{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:12","title":"OnePlus Nord GCam review","link":"https://phandroid.com/?p=255461","description":"<p>After a handful of smartphone camera comparison between the OnePlus Nord and a few flagship devices (<a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/10/oneplus-nord-cant-compete-with-the-pixel-4a-in-camera-comparison/\">and the Pixel 4a</a>), I thought it would be interesting to see if the image quality from the Nord&#8217;s main camera could improve by using the GCam camera app.<p>The OnePlus Nord&#8217;s camera results are really good when you consider that we&#8217;re talking about a mid-range smartphone that costs 400 Euro, but the computational photography wizardry built into Google&#8217;s HDR+ mode in GCam always seems to perform better than stock camera app on most devices.</p><h3 style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/11/how-to-unlock-the-bootloader-and-root-the-oneplus-nord/\">How to unlock the bootloader and root the OnePlus Nord</a></h3><p>Installing the <a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/12/install-gcam-oneplus-nord/\">GCam app on the Oneplus Nord is fairly simple</a>. Since the phone is still new, the ultrawide cameras on the front and back of the phone can&#8217;t yet be used with GCam, but that should change in the coming weeks.</p><p><iframe title=\"OnePlus Nord GCam camera test\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/yLx4ItET_c8?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><p>In most situations, GCam managed to deliver betters images than what you can get from the stock camera app on the OnePlus Nord. The pictures from the stock app are a bit brighter and more saturated, but when you take a closer look, often times the highlights are blown out and subtle details and textures are lost. The GCam&#8217;s computational photography manages to capture better dynamic range, preserving the fine details, delivering more refined photos.</p><p>Google&#8217;s camera app also has the advantage in most low light situations and that&#8217;s also where its Night Sight feature truly comes to life. The Nightscape mode on the Nord is pretty good, but it&#8217;s nowhere near what the GCam can deliver. On the flip side, if you&#8217;re not using the dedicated low light capture mode on either device, the Nord&#8217;s camera performs best in extreme low-light situations. This may change with a few modifications to the GCam all over time, but the Nord has the advantage in this specific scenario.</p><p>As for selfies, it&#8217;s a bit of a mixed bag. The OnePlus Nord&#8217;s stock app performs better in well-lit situations while GCam produces crisper images in portrait mode with better definition between the subject and the background and sharper images when lighting isn&#8217;t optimal.</p><p>There&#8217;s are definite advantages is you have the GCam app installed on the OnePlus Nord, but most of them aren&#8217;t immediately noticeable unless you&#8217;re looking at side-by-side comparisons. Once developers manage to get the ultrawide working, GCam will be a must-have app for every OnePlus Nord owner.</p><h2>OnePlus Nord GCam image samples</h2><p><a Motorola has largely dominated the low-end budget tier with devices like the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Power-Battery1-Unlocked-Motorola-Camera/dp/B084D89DBF/?tag=phndrd-20\" target=\"_blank\">Moto G</a> and <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Moto-Unlocked-Motorola-Camera-XT2052-1/dp/B086H3HH5V/?tag=phndrd-20\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Moto E</a>. But now others are jumping in the fray, including Google with the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07R5CBGY4/?tag=phndrd-20\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel 3a</a> last year and the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Google-Pixel-4a-Unlocked-Smartphone/dp/B08CFSZLQ4/?tag=phndrd-20\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel 4a</a> this year. TCL is also joining the fun with the TCL 10 Pro and 10L.<p>In our review of the TCL 10 Pro, we found that the device is a great buy for $450, considering the spec-sheet and overall design. With a rating of 4.1, you would think that this was a home run, but there were some issues such as battery life and just a mediocre camera system. Nonetheless, it made me excited to test out the TCL 10L, as I&#8217;m intrigued by these devices that are priced at less than $400, which brings us to the TCL 10L.</p><h2>TCL 10L Specifications</h2><ul>\n<li><span>6.53-inch 2340 x 1080 LCD display</span></li>\n<li>Qualcomm Snapdragon<span>&#160;</span><span>665</span></li>\n<li>6GB of RAM</li>\n<li>64GB of storage &#38; microSD card slot</li>\n<li>Quad cameras:<span> 48</span><span>MP (main),&#160;</span><span>8MP (ultrawide), 2</span><span>MP (macro),&#160;</span><span>2MP (depth)</span></li>\n<li>Selfie camera:<span>&#160;</span><span>16MP</span></li>\n<li><span>4,000 mAh battery</span></li>\n<li>Extras: Smart Key, 3.5mm Headphone Jack, Rear-mounted fingerprint scanner</li>\n</ul><h2>Design</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255576\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255576\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255576 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-5-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>When you take the 10L out of the box for the first time, you may be surprised by how absolutely stunning the overall design is. It&#8217;s comfortable in the hand with its rounded corners, the power and volume rocker are in the perfect position on the right-hand frame, and then you flip it over to the back.</p><p>The Mariana Blue color just glimmers and shines every time the light hits it, creating a rainbow effect that left me taking many more pictures of the device than normal. Sticking to the back, you&#8217;ll find the TCL logo planted right in the middle, the quad-camera bump is placed closer to the top, and the fingerprint scanner is placed right in between. There&#8217;s really good symmetry here, another reason why I took too many pictures.</p><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255579\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255579\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255579 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-8-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>As for the rest of the device, you&#8217;ll be surprised and happy to know that TCL opted to include a 3.5mm headphone jack in the 10L, which can be found on the top. The left frame is where you&#8217;ll find the SIM card tray, along with the &#8220;Smart Key&#8221;. Finally, moving to the bottom, we have the USB-C charger flanked by a speaker and microphone array.</p><p>For a device priced at $250, it was so comfortable to hold, that my excitement continued to grow. Sure, it&#8217;s a fingerprint magnet, so you&#8217;ll need to keep a microfiber cloth with you, or you could just use the useful TPU case that is included in the box and has &#8220;Display Greatness&#8221; embossed across the back.</p><h2>Display</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2018/10/15/the-new-palm-is-a-surprisingly-different-android-smartphone/palm-hand/\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-233786\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-233786 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1026\" height=\"870\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand.jpg 1026w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand-350x297.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand-768x651.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand-640x543.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand-800x678.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/10/palm-hand-400x339.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>The 10L and 10 Pro are not first ventures into the smartphone market for TCL, which is better known for its televisions. TCL has had partnerships with Alcatel and BlackBerry and was notably the company behind the purchase of Palm back in 2014. The Palm Phone marked the first device created by a TCL-owned entity, but it&#8217;s clear that the company wants to branch out a bit more than just providing a &#8220;secondary device&#8221; to your main smartphone.</p><p>We bring this up because it&#8217;s important to understand that TCL has some idea of what a smartphone should look like, and one key feature for many is the display. Since the company already has success in the television market, it would only make sense for a TCL smartphone to have a focus on its display.</p><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255586\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255586\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255586 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1334\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10.jpg 2000w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-1536x1025.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-800x534.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-10-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>The display on the TCL 10L measures in at 6.53-inches, with a Full HD+ (2,340 x 1080) resolution along with a hole-punch camera in the top left-hand corner. This brings us to our first disappointment, as LCD panels are not always the greatest, and are largely a frustration when using a device. But at $250, it&#8217;s hard to belabor the point too much.</p><p>Since the 10L has an LCD panel and a 1080p resolution, TCL decided to try and &#8220;game the system&#8221; by adding some software features to improve the display. That&#8217;s where the NXTVision comes into play, which is a dedicated profile to increase sharpness and contrast. Plus, this aims to enhance the dark scenes in videos, but it&#8217;s just not something that I was really interested in. The display&#160;<em>looks<strong>&#160;</strong></em>better with it enabled, but it had too much &#8220;pop&#8221; for my taste.</p><h2>Software</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255580\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255580\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255580 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-9-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>Out of the box, TCL is shipping Android 10, along with a slew of additional software features to try and enhance the experience. There&#8217;s a custom launcher pre-installed, which alphabetizes your App Drawer by default, along with a few pre-installed apps. These include regular culprits, such as Facebook and Netflix, but there are some useful add-ons that you&#8217;ll find once you&#8217;ve finished the initial setup process.</p><p>Some of the shortcuts you&#8217;ll find include a button to lock the screen, quick access to &#8220;Smart Key&#8221; (more on that momentarily), and a few of TCL&#8217;s own apps. You&#8217;ll also find some apps that will make you roll your eyes, such as &#8220;Optimize&#8221; and &#8220;Smart Manager&#8221;, which claim to improve the software, but it just feels like pre-installed anti-malware.</p><p>As you start getting your phone set up and notifications start rolling through, you&#8217;ll notice the edges of your phone light up. If you&#8217;ve used a Samsung device, this may look familiar, although it&#8217;s a bit different. It really is a nice touch, but it&#8217;s more useful when your screen is turned off.</p><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255617\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255617\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255617 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1334\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L.jpg 2000w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-1536x1025.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-800x534.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Options-TCL-10L-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>Opening the Settings app, you&#8217;ll find a slew of different options and toggles to go through and mess around with. Especially if you dive into &#8220;Advanced features&#8221;, where you can adjust the system navigation, switching between gestures or the old-school three on-screen buttons at the bottom. This is separate from the &#8220;Gestures&#8221; settings panel, which houses a few system gestures including enabling the ability to activate split-screen mode with three fingers, or swiping down with three fingers to take a screenshot.</p><p>&#160;</p><p>The final major feature I would like to bring up is the Smart Key that is found on the left frame of the phone and can be customized to your liking. There are three different options when opening the Smart Key settings; single press, double press, or long press. But the absolute best part about this is the fact that each of these is customizable. Here are some of my favorites:</p><ul>\n<li>Assign an app to a &#8220;press&#8221;</li>\n<li>Single press to activate Google Assistant</li>\n<li>Double press to Launch the camera</li>\n<li>Long-press to take a Screenshot (I take a lot of screenshots)</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255618\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255618\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255618 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L-.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1334\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L-.jpg 2000w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--1536x1025.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--800x534.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Smart-Key-Press-Options-TCL-10L--400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>Being able to set a specific app to open with one of those gestures is just amazing. The best part is that any app that you download can be used, so the options are endless. We really wish more OEMs would include a smart button that is user-customizable, but I doubt any flagship devices will launch with one anytime soon.</p><h3>Daily Usage</h3><p>So far, so good for the TCL 10L, right? That&#8217;s how I felt too until it was gone. My apps were installed, I played a few games, and then I realized that the app that I had opened 30 minutes ago, and had only opened two other apps, had to be reloaded. The 6GB of RAM was not enough to keep that app running, which is fine and dandy, but somewhat of a frustration.</p><p>Nonetheless, I kept trucking along with the 10L and then noticed something else. There was a noticeable stutter while doing just about anything with the phone. It&#8217;s almost like the 10L couldn&#8217;t keep up with how fast my finger was gesturing to swipe the screen up to read my Twitter feed. I went into the settings, tried adjusting the NXTVision and Display settings, but came up short.</p><p>This problem has continued sporadically throughout my usage and is a major sore-point for an otherwise solid device. There&#8217;s&#160;<em>just enough</em> lag in usage for it to be noticeable and waiting for the screen to catch up with the swipe is never fun. Maybe my device is a lemon, but I&#8217;ve seen and heard about this same problem cropping up for others who have used the 10L for more than just a day or two.</p><p>Maybe with its next device, TCL can go back to the drawing board for the software and take a Motorola approach. There&#8217;s no need to pre-load a bunch of stuff, just give us a near-stock experience and this is an easy-pick for everyone.</p><h2>Cameras</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255582\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255582\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255582 colorbox-255556\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/TCL-10L-Pro-Review-13-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>By no means am I a great photographer, but I like to take pictures, and was intrigued by the quad-camera array found on the 10L. TCL included a 48MP primary camera, along with an 8MP Ultra Wide sensor, 2MP macro lens, and 2MP depth sensor. On paper, this looked to be a pretty great system, even while lowering expectations because we&#8217;re not going to get  <!--SHR --><a href=\"http://phandroid.com/pixel/\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel</a><!-- EHR -->-level photos out of a TCL product.</p><p>Overall, the pictures were pretty solid, but there was some struggling with the macro lens and auto-focusing. There were a couple of times where I just had to hold the phone because of whatever processing was being done for a basic picture of a flower. And there was an obvious struggle when trying to take pictures at night, but again, we weren&#8217;t expecting the world.</p><p>So did TCL deliver with a solid camera system? Sure? It&#8217;s not going to blow anything else out of the water, but &#8220;more is better&#8221; and while the sensors themselves are just meh, being able to switch between standard, ultrawide, and having a macro lens is always nice. You can check out our photo samples and let us know what you think.</p><h2>Battery</h2><p>With the 4,000mAh battery paired up with Qualcomm&#8217;s Snapdragon 665, battery life is pretty solid, as I was able to push it to about a day and a half. Granted, that&#8217;s not traveling very far or using much GPS, but a day and half of usage is more than adequate and was refreshing, compared to using flagships that need some juice in less than a day.</p><p>The disappointing aspect of the 10L and its battery was in the charging speeds. Unlike the 10 Pro, the 10L does not have Qualcomm&#8217;s QC 3.0 onboard, meaning that you&#8217;re stuck with normal charging speeds. This device is great if you need to practice some patience, but is frustrating if you don&#8217;t care and just want fast charging.</p><h2>Should you get one?</h2><p>If devices like the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Power-Battery1-Unlocked-Motorola-Camera/dp/B084D89DBF/?tag=phndrd-20\" target=\"_blank\">Moto G Power</a> and <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Google-Pixel-4a-Unlocked-Smartphone/dp/B08CFSZLQ4/?tag=phndrd-20\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel 4a</a> weren&#8217;t available, I would still probably recommend the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/TCL-Unlocked-Android-Smartphone-Display/dp/B087LYQ22N?tag=phndrd-20\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">TCL 10L</a>, despite its shortcomings. But unless you really want a design that stands out from the rest, along with great battery life and an array of cameras, those aforementioned devices are the way to go. That&#8217;s not to say the 10L is a bad phone, the software issues just outweigh everything else.</p><p></p><center><a class=\"btn btn-primary btn-lg\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/TCL-Unlocked-Android-Smartphone-Display/dp/B087LYQ22N?tag=phndrd-20\" target=\"_blank\">Buy the TCL 10L</a></center><p>&#160;</p><div class=\"pros-cons-container\">\n<section class=\"pros-cons card\">\n<div class=\"card-title\">\n<h2><span itemprop=\"itemReviewed\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Product\"> <span itemprop=\"name\"> TCL 10L </span> </span> <span itemprop=\"reviewRating\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Rating\" class=\"overall-score right\"> Rating: <i class=\"stars\">star_full</i><i class=\"stars\">star_full</i><i class=\"stars\">star_full</i><i class=\"stars\">star_empty</i><i class=\"stars\">star_empty</i> (<span itemprop=\"ratingValue\">3</span> / <span itemprop=\"bestRating\">5</span>) </span></h2>\n</div>\n<div class=\"card-content\">\n<div class=\"pros\">\n<h3>The Good</h3>\n<ul>\n<li>Gorgeous design</li>\n<li>The display is pretty good</li>\n<li>The more cameras, the better</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<div class=\"cons\">\n<h3>The Bad</h3>\n<ul>\n<li>Consistent lag while in use</li>\n<li>Struggles with auto-focus and night photography</li>\n<li>Too much &#8220;extra stuff&#8221; in the software</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h3>The Bottom Line</h3>\n<p>If TCL can fix the software stuttering, then the 10L would be a fantastic value, coming in at just $250. But for now, you&#8217;re better off picking up the Pixel 4a.</p>\n</div>\n</section>\n</div><p>&#160;</p></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 15 Aug 2020 12:00:01 18:57:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:12","title":"Samsung Galaxy Buds Live First Impressions: Beans are good","link":"https://phandroid.com/?p=255622","description":"<p>As I&#8217;ve <a to my music and podcasts. But, that doesn&#8217;t stop me from loving headphones and wanting to try out just about every set that I can get my hands (and ears) on. Which brings us to the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Samsung-Wireless-Earbuds-Cancelling-Warranty/dp/B089B658NP/?tag=phndrd-20\" rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\">Galaxy Buds Live</a>, which were announced alongside the <a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/05/this-is-the-samsung-galaxy-note-20-and-note-20-ultra/\">Galaxy Note 20 lineup</a> last week. This is not going to be our full review, but just my first impressions as I don&#8217;t feel that I&#8217;ve had enough time with them to formulate a complete review.<p>When the Buds Live first were shown off, I rolled my eyes and thought that there is no way that these would fit into my ears. It&#8217;s not that I have enormous or tiny ears, but the outline of the inner ear itself is what I was concerned with. I was also worried that the earbuds and case were going to end up being larger, due to the addition of ANC along with the interesting and bean-like design. Yes, beans. It&#8217;s what they are, and it&#8217;s awesome. Samsung even printed &#8220;Bean&#8221; on the <a href=\"https://www.ifixit.com/Teardown/Samsung+Galaxy+Buds+Live+Teardown/135908\">inside of the earbuds</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255624\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255624\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255624 colorbox-255622\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1333\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2.jpg 2000w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-1600x1066.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-2-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>To my pleasure, I was greeted with a tiny box, with an even smaller case, and some really cute-looking earbuds. Instead, these are designed to just nestle inside of your ear-lobe, with the earpiece facing downwards into your ear canal.</p><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/?attachment_id=255626\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255626\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255626 colorbox-255622\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1333\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4.jpg 2000w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-1600x1066.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Samsung-Galaxy-Buds-Live-First-Impressions-4-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>Another cause for concern that I had came with worrying if the Buds Live would actually stay in my ears. Now, I&#8217;m not a runner and I don&#8217;t go to the gym, but I do like to wear my headphones while I&#8217;m running errands or grabbing some groceries. So if the Buds Live would fall out, that would be an instant deal-breaker, regardless of how great they sounded. To my pleasure, the little ear-tip installed around the charging pins helps to keep the Buds Live in place, and there&#8217;s a large set in the box if you are having issues.</p><p>Setting them up and putting them in is pretty simple, and Samsung doesn&#8217;t have some convoluted method for updating the software, so we don&#8217;t have to worry about another <a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/07/20/google-pixel-buds-review/\">Pixel Buds</a> situation. There&#8217;s an equalizer right on the front page of the Buds Live settings panel, and above that is a toggle for Active Noise Cancellation.</p><p>Without revealing too much, I can definitely say that my <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Apple-MWP22AM-A-AirPods-Pro/dp/B07ZPC9QD4/?tag=phndrd-20\" target=\"_blank\">AirPods Pro</a> is going to continue being the champion earbuds for noise cancellation, as the Buds Live seem to just muffle the sound. This likely has everything to do with the open-ear design of the Buds Live, but at least Samsung provided ANC as an option, which is a nice touch. There are a few other nice features available in the Wearables app to assist in customizing your new headphones with your preferences.</p><p>So far, I&#8217;m enjoying my experience with the Galaxy Beans, I&#8217;m just hoping it stays that way over the next week or two while working on the full review. With foldable phones gaining traction, such as the upcoming Galaxy Fold 2 and the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Samsung-Unlocked-Smartphone-Technology-Long-Lasting/dp/B08DP5BZK4/?tag=andro084-20\" target=\"_blank\">Galaxy Z Flip 5G</a>, there is definitely a market for smartphones that aren&#8217;t just a simple slab of glass anymore.<p><iframe title=\"The new Surface&#160;Duo. Do one better.\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CqRKOY4Cgvw?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p><p>The Microsoft Surface Duo offers a different take on the foldable smartphone, however, giving us a design closer to that of the <a href=\"https://phandroid.com/zte-axon-m/\">ZTE Axon M</a>. That phone never caught on and has become a thing of the past, but this design gives you a general idea of where Microsoft went with its smartphone.e</p><h2>Older specs</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2019/10/02/microsoft-embraces-android-with-its-dual-screen-folding-surface-duo-smartphone/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming/\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-246004\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-246004 colorbox-255548\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1800\" height=\"982\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming.jpg 1800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-350x191.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-768x419.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-640x349.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-1600x873.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-1200x655.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-800x436.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming-400x218.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>So while much of the market (outside of Samsung) is shifting to budget-minded devices like the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Google-Pixel-4a-Unlocked-Smartphone/dp/B08CFSZLQ4?tag=andro084-20\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel 4a</a> and <a href=\"https://www.gearbest.com/cell-phones/pp_009324164803.html?wid=1349303&#38;lkid=79671619\" rel=\"nofollow\">OnePlus Nord</a>, Microsoft is coming out of the gates &#8220;swinging&#8221;. But instead of offering a real home run hitter, the Surface Duo looks just like a ground ball to short.</p><h3>Surface Duo Specs</h3><ul>\n<li>Dual 5.6-inch AMOLED displays; Combined: 8.1-inch</li>\n<li>Qualcomm Snapdragon 855</li>\n<li>6GB of RAM</li>\n<li>128GB / 256GB of storage</li>\n<li>11MP Primary Camera</li>\n<li>3,577mAh battery</li>\n</ul><p>We can forgive the inclusion of the Snapdragon 855 due to the fact that Microsoft has been working on this device for some time. The final design was already finalized and then it had to be put into production, along with passing the quality checks necessary for a phone as venturous as this.</p><p>What is disappointing is the subpar battery size, the inclusion of just 6GB of RAM, and the lack of expandable storage. It&#8217;s clear just from the spec sheet that this is more of an enthusiast device, instead of something that could take over the mainstream. Microsoft is hoping that you use the Surface Duo for productivity, but you could run into some bottle-necking with the older CPU and 6GB of RAM.</p><h2>Just one camera?</h2><p>It&#8217;s not that Microsoft only included a single camera on the Surface Duo. Just look at the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0875RT5WS/?tag=andro084-20\" target=\"_blank\">iPhone SE 2</a> or the  <!--SHR --><a href=\"http://phandroid.com/pixel/\" target=\"_blank\">Pixel</a><!-- EHR --> 4a, and that can be forgiven, even though the Duo you could buy four Pixel 4a&#8217;s and then strap them together for the Ultimate Pixel.</p><p>No, the single-camera system is bothersome because the quality won&#8217;t come even close to whatever Google, Apple, or Samsung are doing with smartphone cameras. It&#8217;s disappointing, to say the least because you&#8217;ll likely still want to carry another smartphone around with you to take solid pictures when the opportunities arise.</p><h2>Lack of future-proofing</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2019/10/02/microsoft-embraces-android-with-its-dual-screen-folding-surface-duo-smartphone/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen/\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-246009\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-246009 colorbox-255548\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1800\" height=\"982\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen.jpg 1800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-350x191.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-768x419.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-640x349.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-1600x873.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-1200x655.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-800x436.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen-400x218.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>So there&#8217;s more than one reason why Microsoft opted to stick with the Snapdragon 855, instead of moving to even the 855+ SoC. Starting with the SD865, Qualcomm has mandated that OEM&#8217;s using the 865 must also include a separate 5G processor.</p><p>The design for the Duo was finalized long before the 865 made its way onto the market, and it would have required Microsoft to go back to the design-board far too late in the process. So that means your brand-new phone won&#8217;t be able to take advantage of 5G.</p><p>Coming back around to productivity, 6GB of RAM for a flagship-level device won&#8217;t stand up against the test of time. It&#8217;s&#160;<em>fine</em> for now, but it likely won&#8217;t hold up over the next few years.</p><h2>The basics aren&#8217;t build-in</h2><p>So you&#8217;re already sacrificing performance and the lack of future-proofing with no 5G on board. But there are a few &#8220;basics&#8221; that also weren&#8217;t included with the Duo. You can, probably, get over the lack of wireless charging for a first-gen device, but in a world where contactless payments are paramount, no NFC is a head-scratcher.</p><p>Sure, Microsoft could never anticipate the global climate of 2020, but even still. Not being even being able to tap an NFC tag or use your phone in the checkout line is something that is just frustrating overall. Maybe it doesn&#8217;t matter that much because again, this is a first-gen device, but it&#8217;s an annoying omission.</p><p>Finally, while it&#8217;s great that Microsoft is including either 128GB or 256GB of storage, that&#8217;s all you get. There&#8217;s no built-in microSD card slot, but the Surface Duo did include a dual-SIM system with a Nano-SIM and eSIM, but that &#8220;space&#8221; could have been used for a microSD card slot.</p><h2>That price tag</h2><p>All of this brings us to the price. We had to save the best (worst) for last, right? The Surface Duo will be released on September 10th for an eye-watering $1400. That&#8217;s a dual-display device that is featuring two-year-old specs and is missing some key features.</p><p>Those wanting to pre-order one can trade in their current device, potentially knocking the price in half. But as we mentioned before, do you really want to give up your current flagship for an experimental first-gen product? Probably not. So if you really want to get your hands on the Duo, it will cost more than the brand-new <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Samsung-Factory-Unlocked-Smartphone-Long-Lasting/dp/B08BX7QGKF/?tag=andro084-20\" target=\"_blank\">Galaxy Note 20 Ultra</a> and is just $50 less than the new Galaxy Z Flip 5G.</p></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 13 Aug 2020 16:00:17 +0000","feedId":333,"bgimg":"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming.jpg","linkMd5":"de92e2e8624ccafe0a4fa6125010fdbf","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn57@2020_6/2020/08/16/10-57-15-684_dc3b0332a4b93e4f.webp","destWidth":1800,"destHeight":982,"author":"Andrew","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-gaming.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn22@2020_3/2020/08/16/10-57-15-101_dc3b0332a4b93e4f.webp","https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/microsoft-surface-duo-home-screen.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn7@2020_5/2020/08/16/10-57-14-530_52bb15e04a108850.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:13","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:13","title":"How to install GCam on the OnePlus Nord","link":"https://phandroid.com/?p=255515","description":"<p>The OnePlus Nord is a spectacular mid-range smartphone and one of the best devices we&#8217;ve used in 2020. rooted. Those days are long gone, but the rooting community has continued to flourish in recent years &#8212; especially thanks to devices like the <a href=\"https://phandroid.com/guide/oneplus-nord/\">OnePlus Nord</a>, which makes it easy to root and enjoy the true open-source nature of Android.<p>If you want to try out some new root-only apps or install completely different firmware, you&#8217;ll need to unlock the bootloader and then root your device. Luckily, it&#8217;s an easy process and one that shouldn&#8217;t take too long.</p><h2>What&#8217;s needed before getting started</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/11/how-to-unlock-the-bootloader-and-root-the-oneplus-nord/oneplus-nord-developer-options/\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255445\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255445 colorbox-255442\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p><strong>WARNING: Rooting the OnePlus Nord may void your warranty and may cause damage to your device if done incorrectly. Proceed at your own risk. </strong></p><p>As is the case whenever you are modifying your smartphone, there are a few steps that need to be taken before you can get your hands dirty. It&#8217;s also important to note that during the process of unlocking the bootloader and rooting your OnePlus Nord, your device will be completely wiped. So make sure that your all of your important files are backed up safely, including your photos, downloads, and anything else that you want to keep.</p><ol>\n<li><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/backup-android/\">Backup</a> your device.</li>\n<li>Install OxygenOS version 10.5.2 onto your Nord (<strong><a href=\"https://forum.xda-developers.com/oneplus-nord/how-to/oneplus-nord-repo-oxygen-os-builds-t4138085\">here</a></strong>).</li>\n<li>Download and install the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/releases/platform-tools\">Android SDK Platform Tools</a> onto your PC.</li>\n</ol><p>Once you have the SDK installed, and your Nord is updated to version 10.5.2 of OxygenOS, there are a few more steps you need to take. However, these are done right on your smartphone.</p><ol>\n<li>Open the Settings app.</li>\n<li>Scroll down and tap&#160;<strong>About Phone</strong>.</li>\n<li>Tap on the&#160;<strong>Build Number</strong> seven (7) times to enable Developer Options.</li>\n<li>Go back to Settings.</li>\n<li>Scroll down and select&#160;<strong>System</strong>.</li>\n<li>Tap&#160;<strong>Advanced</strong>.</li>\n<li>Tap&#160;<strong>Developer Options</strong>.</li>\n<li>Tap the toggle next to&#160;<strong>OEM Unlocking</strong> and&#160;<strong>USB Debugging</strong>.</li>\n</ol><p>Now you are all set and ready to unlock the bootloader and root your OnePlus Nord!</p><h2>How to unlock the OnePlus Nord bootloader</h2><p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/2020/08/11/how-to-unlock-the-bootloader-and-root-the-oneplus-nord/oneplus-nord-usb-debugging-up-close/\" rel=\"attachment wp-att-255446\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-255446 colorbox-255442\" src=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2500\" height=\"1667\" srcset=\"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close.jpg 2500w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-350x233.jpg 350w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-640x427.jpg 640w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-768x512.jpg 768w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-1536x1024.jpg 1536w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-2048x1366.jpg 2048w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-1600x1067.jpg 1600w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-1200x800.jpg 1200w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-800x533.jpg 800w, https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close-400x267.jpg 400w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 480px) 25vw, (max-width: 780px) 40vw, (max-width: 1080px) 30vw, (max-width: 1280px) 30vw, (max-width: 1600px) 30vw, 800px\"></a></p><p>Once you&#8217;ve enabled Developer Options and flipped the switch for OEM Unlocking and USB Debugging, you are ready to unlock the bootloader. This is just the first step of the process, but it will wipe your Nord completely, so we want to re-iterate to backup any important or pertinent files before they are lost.</p><ol>\n<li>Connect your OnePlus Nord to your PC with the OnePlus Cable, if possible.</li>\n<li>Open the <strong>Command Window</strong> on your PC.</li>\n<li>Boot into fast mode by entering the following into the Command/Terminal Window:\n<ul>\n<li><strong><em>adb reboot bootloader</em></strong></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>Unlock the bootloader by entering the following into the Command/Terminal Window:\n<ul>\n<li><strong><em>fastboot oem unlock</em></strong></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ol><p>Once completed, your Nord should be rebooted and then you will need to go through the OxygenOS setup process. From there, your bootloader will be unlocked, and you can proceed with rooting your device.</p><h2>How to root the OnePlus Nord</h2><p>Another couple of steps that you&#8217;ll need to take before being able to root the Nord is to have the latest version of the Magisk Manager installed, along with the stock firmware available. This can be downloaded <strong><a href=\"https://github.com/topjohnwu/Magisk/releases/download/manager-v7.5.1/MagiskManager-v7.5.1.apk\">here</a></strong>&#160;and should be downloaded and installed directly onto your device. As for the stock firmware (AKA boot.img), this needs to be downloaded (<a href=\"https://drive.google.com/file/d/18aPqErEMbRqmN4BpdvHE4OKgizDcEbou/view?usp=sharing\" rel=\"nofollow\"><strong>from here</strong></a>) and placed somewhere easily accessible in your file manager.</p><p>Once both the Magisk Manager and the boot.img have been downloaded, you can get started.</p><ol>\n<li>Install the Magisk Manager application that was previously downloaded.</li>\n<li>Open the app, and choose&#160;<strong>Select and patch a file</strong>.</li>\n<li>Choose the stock firmware (boot.img) file that was downloaded.</li>\n<li>Once complete, the patched firmware will be available in the Downloads folder on your device.</li>\n<li>With your OnePlus Nord plugged into the computer, transfer the patched boot.img to the PC.</li>\n<li>From your computer, open the Command Window and type the following:\n<ul>\n<li><strong><em>adb reboot bootloader</em></strong></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>Once in Fastboot Mode, type the following into the Command Window:\n<ul>\n<li><em>f<strong>astboot getvar current-slot</strong></em>\n<ul>\n<li>If the output is &#8220;a&#8221;, type <span><strong><em>fastboot flash boot_a magisk_patched.img</em></strong> and press Enter.</span></li>\n<li>If the output is &#8220;b&#8221;, type <em><strong>fastboot flash boot_b magisk_patched.img</strong></em>&#160;and press Enter.</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>Reboot your OnePlus Nord.</li>\n</ol><p>Once rebooted, go back and open the Magisk Manager application again. The app should now show whether your device was successfully rooted or not. If not, repeat the steps from the beginning, ensuring that all of the commands have been properly entered.</p><h5>Source: <a href=\"https://www.xda-developers.com/how-to-root-unlock-bootloader-oneplus-nord-magisk/\">XDA Developers</a></h5></p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 11 Aug 2020 21:00:00 +0000","feedId":333,"bgimg":"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options.jpg","linkMd5":"89297b8ea4f0ff68b6a33143975a128b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx17/cdn49@2020_2/2020/08/16/10-57-16-399_0f0bba1d065404f1.webp","destWidth":2500,"destHeight":1667,"author":"Andrew","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-Developer-Options.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx20/cdn49@2020_3/2020/08/16/10-57-18-213_0f0bba1d065404f1.webp","https://phandroid.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/OnePlus-Nord-USB-Debugging-Up-Close.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn93@2020_6/2020/08/16/10-57-18-631_ffdc548c2f1239e4.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:12","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:57:12","title":"Best fitness trackers in 2020","link":"https://phandroid.com/?p=250277","description":"<p><a href=\"https://phandroid.com/guide/wear-os/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Wear OS</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is showing signs of life again in 2020 with the Qualcomm Snapdragon Wear 4100 platform possibly delivering the performance and efficiency that has been missing, but for many of us, a fitness tracker is still the better wearable option to pair with our Android phones. better battery life.&#160;</span><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Let&#8217;s take a look at some of the top options in the market today, regardless of your goals with a wearable there is likely Garmin uses this data to produce a Body Battery score that is meant to give you an idea of when to exercise versus when you should be perhaps trying to recover energy.</span></p><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Vivosmart 4 supports text, call, and app notifications and like the Galaxy Fit you can customize some quick replies if you are unable to access your smartphone.&#160;</span></p><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fitness tracking is solid with a number of activities that will be automatically recognized and tracked by Move IQ, such as walking, swimming, cycling, running or elliptical training and a number of other activities that can be triggered manually. It later got upgraded where it could support CDs, and then we started to see more car manufacturers introduce displays where more information could be displayed and where it could even be used to stream a video when you are reversing.<p>These days, <a href=\"https://www.wapcar.my/\">our cars</a> are getting smarter with technology like Google&#8217;s Android Auto system, allowing us to connect our phones to our cars for expanded capabilities with a more familiar operating system.</p><p>For those who are unfamiliar, Android Auto is basically Google&#8217;s answer to car infotainment systems, where instead of each car maker using their own software, Android Auto (which is based on Android), offers a more familiar interface as well as apps that you already know and use, like Google Maps, Google Messages, and more.</p><p>So why would you choose to use Android Auto over the default system loaded by the carmaker? For starters, safety. Due to the fact that Android Auto is linked and synced with our smartphones, it means that drivers can focus more on driving and less on their phones. Information from our phones, like incoming calls or messages, can now be shown on the display of an Android Auto unit. You can also control and interact with them via controls on your steering wheel (if supported by the car maker).</p><p>Also, since Android Auto is based on Android, you will also be able to access features like Google Assistant, where you can use your voice to interact with your device like to make calls, send messages, navigate, and so on. Most laptops are not in such dire shape, but SD card readers, Ethernet jacks, and HDMI ports are almost always missing from the newest ultralights.<p>USB-C hubs are a dime a dozen, but almost all of them have major limitations. They&#8217;ll limit your charging abilities to somewhere around 65 watts, which is fine for many notebooks but not enough for some. And almost every time, the HDMI port only supports output at 4K30, and 4K30 isn&#8217;t very usable with a computer.</p><p><img class=\"colorbox-255538\" src=\"https://ksr-ugc.imgix.net/assets/029/920/639/1e33d28e1279cdbfb60a0bd221351ca2_original.gif?ixlib=rb-2.1.0&#38;w=680&#38;fit=max&#38;v=1595498609&#38;auto=format&#38;gif-q=50&#38;q=92&#38;s=ca2e175d8eac801cedb335c01feba23b\"></p><p>Lauco aims to change that with what they call the &#8220;smallest and most powerful&#8221; USB-C charging hub around. These hubs are made out of tempered glass and aluminum alloy. There are two versions, an 8-in-1 and a larger 12-in-1. Both feature up to 100W charging (85W at the laptop and the rest reserved for other functions), a 10W wireless charger on top, a 4K60 HDMI port, dual USB-C 3.0 5Gbps ports, a USB-A 3.0 5Gbps port, and an SD/microSD UHS-1 card reader. The larger version adds a second 4K60 HDMI port (though they run at 4K30 each when both used), two extra USB-A 3.0 ports, and a 1Gbps Ethernet jack. The smaller is around 85 x 130mm while the larger one is around 105 x 170mm.</p><p>Besides being used for a laptop, you can also use it with your phone if it features a desktop mode. And when not in use as a hub, you can use it as a plain old wireless charger. Even when you&#8217;re not near an outlet, this hub can wirelessly charge your phone at five watts when plugged into a computer. This hub packs a ton of features into a surprisingly small package and will make for a great travel accessory.</p><p>The Kickstarter for the Lauco hub has just launched and you can still pick up your choice of hub for 50% off. An 8-in-1 hub will cost you $59 while the 12-in-1 will cost you $75. After those limited pledges are taken up the price goes up to $69 and $89 respectively. Both also come with a short and beefy C to C cable as well as a drawstring pouch for keeping it safe.
